	<h1 id="firstHeading" class="firstHeading" lang="en">Subway (restaurant)</h1>

<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:1301_NE_Broadway_-_Irvington_HD_-_Portland_Oregon.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/d3/1301_NE_Broadway_-_Irvington_HD_-_Portland_Oregon.jpg/220px-1301_NE_Broadway_-_Irvington_HD_-_Portland_Oregon.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="165" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/d3/1301_NE_Broadway_-_Irvington_HD_-_Portland_Oregon.jpg/330px-1301_NE_Broadway_-_Irvington_HD_-_Portland_Oregon.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/d3/1301_NE_Broadway_-_Irvington_HD_-_Portland_Oregon.jpg/440px-1301_NE_Broadway_-_Irvington_HD_-_Portland_Oregon.jpg 2x" data-file-width="4032" data-file-height="3024" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:1301_NE_Broadway_-_Irvington_HD_-_Portland_Oregon.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Subway restaurant in <a href="/wiki/Portland,_Oregon" title="Portland, Oregon">Portland, Oregon</a></div></div></div>
<p><b>Subway</b> is an American privately held  <a href="/wiki/Fast_food_restaurant" title="Fast food restaurant">restaurant</a> <a href="/wiki/Franchising" title="Franchising">franchise</a> that primarily sells <a href="/wiki/Submarine_sandwich" title="Submarine sandwich">submarine sandwiches</a> (subs) and <a href="/wiki/Salad" title="Salad">salads</a>. It is one of the fastest-growing franchises in the world<sup id="cite_ref-Herold_2015_2-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Herold_2015-2">&#91;2&#93;</a></sup> and, as of June 2017, had approximately 42,000 locations in more than 100 countries. More than half of the locations are in the United States.<sup id="cite_ref-SubwayLocations_1-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-SubwayLocations-1">&#91;1&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-3" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-3">&#91;3&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-Statista_4-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Statista-4">&#91;4&#93;</a></sup> It also is the largest single-brand restaurant chain, and the largest restaurant operator, in the world.<sup id="cite_ref-Subway_5-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Subway-5">&#91;5&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-Food_&amp;_Wine_2017_6-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Food_&amp;_Wine_2017-6">&#91;6&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-mcds_7-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-mcds-7">&#91;7&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-8" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-8">&#91;8&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>As of 2017<sup class="plainlinks noexcerpt noprint asof-tag update" style="display:none;"><a class="external text" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=Subway_(restaurant)&amp;action=edit">&#91;update&#93;</a></sup>, the Subway Group of companies was organized as follows:
</p>
<ul><li>Subway IP Inc. is the owner of the intellectual property for the restaurant system.</li>
<li>Franchise World Headquarters, LLC leads franchising operations. FWH Technologies, LLC owns and licenses Subway's <a href="/wiki/Point_of_sale" title="Point of sale">point of sale</a> software.</li>
<li>Franchisors include Doctor's Associates Inc. in the U.S.; Subway International B.V.; Subway Franchise Systems of Canada, Ltd.; etc.</li>
<li>Advertising affiliates include Subway Franchisee Advertising Fund Trust, Ltd.; Subway Franchisee Advertising Fund Trust, B.V.; Subway Franchisee Canadian Advertising Trust; etc.<sup id="cite_ref-9" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-9">&#91;9&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-10" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-10">&#91;10&#93;</a></sup></li></ul>
<p>Subway's international headquarters are in <a href="/wiki/Milford,_Connecticut" title="Milford, Connecticut">Milford, Connecticut</a>, with five regional centers supporting the company's international operations. The regional offices for European franchises are located in <a href="/wiki/Amsterdam" title="Amsterdam">Amsterdam</a> (Netherlands); the <a href="/wiki/Australia" title="Australia">Australian</a> and <a href="/wiki/New_Zealand" title="New Zealand">New Zealand</a> locations are supported from <a href="/wiki/Brisbane" title="Brisbane">Brisbane</a> (Australia); the Asian locations are supported from offices in <a href="/wiki/Beirut" title="Beirut">Beirut</a> (Lebanon) and <a href="/wiki/Singapore" title="Singapore">Singapore</a>; and the Latin American support center is in <a href="/wiki/Miami" title="Miami">Miami</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-11" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-11">&#91;11&#93;</a></sup>
</p>

logo used from 2002 to 2016 (still used on signage in many locations)</div></div></div></div></div>
<p>In 1965, <a href="/wiki/Fred_DeLuca" title="Fred DeLuca">Fred DeLuca</a> borrowed $1,000 from friend <a href="/wiki/Peter_Buck_(restaurateur)" title="Peter Buck (restaurateur)">Peter Buck</a> to start "Pete's Super Submarines" in <a href="/wiki/Bridgeport,_Connecticut" title="Bridgeport, Connecticut">Bridgeport, Connecticut</a>, and in the following year, they formed Doctor's Associates Inc. to oversee operations of the restaurants as the franchise expanded.<sup id="cite_ref-History_12-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-History-12">&#91;12&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-WashingtonPost_13-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-WashingtonPost-13">&#91;13&#93;</a></sup> The holding company derives its name from DeLuca's goal to earn enough from the business to pay tuition for medical school, as well as Buck's having a doctorate in physics.<sup id="cite_ref-BOWDOINLHD_14-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-BOWDOINLHD-14">&#91;14&#93;</a></sup> Doctor's Associates is not affiliated with, nor endorsed by, any medical organization.<sup id="cite_ref-15" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-15">&#91;15&#93;</a></sup> In 1968, the sandwich shop was renamed "Subway".<sup id="cite_ref-History_12-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-History-12">&#91;12&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Subway_restaurant_Pittsfield_Township_Michigan.JPG" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/5d/Subway_restaurant_Pittsfield_Township_Michigan.JPG/220px-Subway_restaurant_Pittsfield_Township_Michigan.JPG" decoding="async" width="220" height="146" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/5d/Subway_restaurant_Pittsfield_Township_Michigan.JPG/330px-Subway_restaurant_Pittsfield_Township_Michigan.JPG 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/5d/Subway_restaurant_Pittsfield_Township_Michigan.JPG/440px-Subway_restaurant_Pittsfield_Township_Michigan.JPG 2x" data-file-width="4715" data-file-height="3133" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Subway_restaurant_Pittsfield_Township_Michigan.JPG" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Subway restaurant in <a href="/wiki/Pittsfield_Township,_Michigan" class="mw-redirect" title="Pittsfield Township, Michigan">Pittsfield Township, Michigan</a> (2011)</div></div></div>
<p>The first Subway on the <a href="/wiki/West_Coast_of_the_United_States" title="West Coast of the United States">West Coast</a> was opened in <a href="/wiki/Fresno,_California" title="Fresno, California">Fresno, California</a>, in 1978.<sup id="cite_ref-16" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-16">&#91;16&#93;</a></sup> The first Subway outside of <a href="/wiki/North_America" title="North America">North America</a> opened in <a href="/wiki/Bahrain" title="Bahrain">Bahrain</a> in December 1984.<sup id="cite_ref-17" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-17">&#91;17&#93;</a></sup> The first Subway in the <a href="/wiki/United_Kingdom" title="United Kingdom">United Kingdom</a> was opened in <a href="/wiki/Brighton" title="Brighton">Brighton</a> in 1996.<sup id="cite_ref-18" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-18">&#91;18&#93;</a></sup> In 2004, Subway began opening stores in <a href="/wiki/Walmart" title="Walmart">Walmart</a> supercenters and surpassed the number of <a href="/wiki/McDonald%27s" title="McDonald&#39;s">McDonald's</a> locations inside U.S. Walmart stores in 2007.<sup id="cite_ref-19" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-19">&#91;19&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>Since 2007, Subway has consistently ranked in <i><a href="/wiki/Entrepreneur_(magazine)" title="Entrepreneur (magazine)">Entrepreneur</a></i> magazine's Top 500 Franchises list. In 2015, it ranked #3 on the "Top Global Franchises" list and #1 as the "Fastest Growing Franchise".<sup id="cite_ref-20" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-20">&#91;20&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-21" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-21">&#91;21&#93;</a></sup> At the end of 2010, Subway became the largest fast food chain worldwide, with 33,749 restaurants&#160;– 1,012 more than <a href="/wiki/McDonald%27s" title="McDonald&#39;s">McDonald's</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-Subway_Runs_Past_McDonald&#39;s_Chain_22-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Subway_Runs_Past_McDonald&#39;s_Chain-22">&#91;22&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Subway_in_Stanhope,_NJ.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/b/bb/Subway_in_Stanhope%2C_NJ.jpg/220px-Subway_in_Stanhope%2C_NJ.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="165" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/b/bb/Subway_in_Stanhope%2C_NJ.jpg/330px-Subway_in_Stanhope%2C_NJ.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/b/bb/Subway_in_Stanhope%2C_NJ.jpg/440px-Subway_in_Stanhope%2C_NJ.jpg 2x" data-file-width="4032" data-file-height="3024" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Subway_in_Stanhope,_NJ.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Subway restaurant in <a href="/wiki/Stanhope,_New_Jersey" title="Stanhope, New Jersey">Stanhope, New Jersey</a> (2018)</div></div></div>
<p>In January 2015, <a href="/wiki/Suzanne_Greco" title="Suzanne Greco">Suzanne Greco</a> became president and CEO after her brother Fred DeLuca, the company’s first CEO, died of leukemia in September 2015 after being ill for two years.<sup id="cite_ref-23" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-23">&#91;23&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-24" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-24">&#91;24&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>In 2016, Subway closed hundreds of restaurants in the U.S., experiencing a net loss in locations for the first time. However, with 26,744 locations, it remained the most ubiquitous restaurant chain in the U.S. (with McDonald's in the #2 spot).<sup id="cite_ref-25" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-25">&#91;25&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Counter_and_customers,_new-style_Subway_restaurant.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/9d/Counter_and_customers%2C_new-style_Subway_restaurant.jpg/220px-Counter_and_customers%2C_new-style_Subway_restaurant.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="165" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/9d/Counter_and_customers%2C_new-style_Subway_restaurant.jpg/330px-Counter_and_customers%2C_new-style_Subway_restaurant.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/9d/Counter_and_customers%2C_new-style_Subway_restaurant.jpg/440px-Counter_and_customers%2C_new-style_Subway_restaurant.jpg 2x" data-file-width="3264" data-file-height="2448" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Counter_and_customers,_new-style_Subway_restaurant.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Interior of a Subway franchise in <a href="/wiki/Huntington,_Virginia" title="Huntington, Virginia">Huntington, Virginia</a> designed in the new style.</div></div></div>
<p>Also in 2016, Subway announced a new logo for the franchise, to be implemented in 2017.<sup id="cite_ref-26" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-26">&#91;26&#93;</a></sup> On July 17, 2017, Subway unveiled redesigned restaurants, dubbed "Fresh Forward." Features include self-order kiosks; USB charging ports at tables; and new menu items, including additional condiments, and bread <a href="/wiki/Gluten_free_diet" class="mw-redirect" title="Gluten free diet">made without gluten</a>. The company is piloting the changes at 12 locations across the United States, Canada, and the United Kingdom, with many features expected to be implemented into stores worldwide by the end of 2017.<sup id="cite_ref-Fresh_Forward_27-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Fresh_Forward-27">&#91;27&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>In 2017, the chain closed more than 800 of its U.S. locations. In April 2018, the chain announced it would close about 500 more that year. According Abha Bhattarai of <i><a href="/wiki/The_Washington_Post" title="The Washington Post">The Washington Post</a></i>, this is a result of three consecutive years of falling profits, and foot traffic in Subway stores reduced by 25 percent since 2012. Franchisees also complained that the company's deep promotions further ate away at profits. Industry analysts like Bob Phibbs, chief executive of the New York-based consulting firm Retail Doctor, say changing tastes on the part of consumers, who more frequently prefer locally sourced produce and hormone-free meat served by regional start-ups like <a href="/wiki/Sweetgreen" title="Sweetgreen">Sweetgreen</a>, especially in metropolitan areas, are the cause of the drop in Subway's sales, as well as loss of market share to competitors. These include fast-casual eateries and sandwich shops like <a href="/wiki/Panera_Bread" title="Panera Bread">Panera Bread</a>, <a href="/wiki/Au_Bon_Pain" title="Au Bon Pain">Au Bon Pain</a> and <a href="/wiki/Firehouse_Subs" title="Firehouse Subs">Firehouse Subs</a>, as well as food trucks, and grocery stores that offer freshly made meals at competitive prices. In January 2018, Subway invested $25 million in a re-branding campaign targeted at young consumers in order to revitalize its image and boost sales.<sup id="cite_ref-WashingtonPost_13-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-WashingtonPost-13">&#91;13&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Locations">Locations</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Subway_(restaurant)&amp;action=edit&amp;section=2" title="Edit section: Locations">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<div class="thumb tleft"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:List_Of_Countries_With_Subway_Restaurants.png" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/64/List_Of_Countries_With_Subway_Restaurants.png/220px-List_Of_Countries_With_Subway_Restaurants.png" decoding="async" width="220" height="102" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/64/List_Of_Countries_With_Subway_Restaurants.png/330px-List_Of_Countries_With_Subway_Restaurants.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/64/List_Of_Countries_With_Subway_Restaurants.png/440px-List_Of_Countries_With_Subway_Restaurants.png 2x" data-file-width="1357" data-file-height="628" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:List_Of_Countries_With_Subway_Restaurants.png" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div><div class="legend" style="-webkit-column-break-inside: avoid;page-break-inside: avoid;break-inside: avoid-column"><span class="legend-color" style="display:inline-block; width:1.5em; height:1.5em; margin:1px 0; border:1px solid black; background-color: #005542; color:black; font-size:100%; text-align:center;">&#160;</span>&#160;Countries with Subway Restaurants</div><div class="legend" style="-webkit-column-break-inside: avoid;page-break-inside: avoid;break-inside: avoid-column"><span class="legend-color" style="display:inline-block; width:1.5em; height:1.5em; margin:1px 0; border:1px solid black; background-color: #00FFFF; color:black; font-size:100%; text-align:center;">&#160;</span>&#160;Countries with plans for Subway Restaurants</div><div class="legend" style="-webkit-column-break-inside: avoid;page-break-inside: avoid;break-inside: avoid-column"><span class="legend-color" style="display:inline-block; width:1.5em; height:1.5em; margin:1px 0; border:1px solid black; background-color: #FF5732; color:black; font-size:100%; text-align:center;">&#160;</span>&#160;Countries that formerly had Subway Restaurants</div></div></div></div>
<p>As of June 2017, Subway had approximately 42,000 locations in 111 countries worldwide, all independently owned.<sup id="cite_ref-WashingtonPost_13-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-WashingtonPost-13">&#91;13&#93;</a></sup> These locations are largely concentrated in North America, with 24,350 in the United States,<sup id="cite_ref-28" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-28">&#91;28&#93;</a></sup> 3,155 in Canada, and 929 in Mexico;<sup id="cite_ref-ExploreOurWorld_29-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-ExploreOurWorld-29">&#91;29&#93;</a></sup> this is almost as many U.S. locations as McDonald’s and Starbucks combined.<sup id="cite_ref-WashingtonPost_13-3" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-WashingtonPost-13">&#91;13&#93;</a></sup> Outside North America, the countries with the most locations are Australia (approximately 1,400), Brazil (approximately 2,200), and the United Kingdom (approximately 2,300).<sup id="cite_ref-ExploreOurWorld_29-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-ExploreOurWorld-29">&#91;29&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Products">Products</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Subway_(restaurant)&amp;action=edit&amp;section=3" title="Edit section: Products">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Subwaysandwich.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/d4/Subwaysandwich.jpg/220px-Subwaysandwich.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="172" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/d4/Subwaysandwich.jpg/330px-Subwaysandwich.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/d4/Subwaysandwich.jpg/440px-Subwaysandwich.jpg 2x" data-file-width="586" data-file-height="459" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Subwaysandwich.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>A Subway Club 6" sandwich</div></div></div>
<p>Subway's core product is the <a href="/wiki/Submarine_sandwich" title="Submarine sandwich">submarine sandwich</a> (or "sub"). In addition to these, the chain also sells <a href="/wiki/Wrap_(sandwich)" class="mw-redirect" title="Wrap (sandwich)">wraps</a>, <a href="/wiki/Salad" title="Salad">salad</a>, <a href="/wiki/Panini_(sandwich)" title="Panini (sandwich)">paninis</a>, and baked goods (including <a href="/wiki/Cookie" title="Cookie">cookies</a>, <a href="/wiki/Doughnut" title="Doughnut">doughnuts</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Muffin" title="Muffin">muffins</a>).
</p><p>Subway's best-selling sandwich,<sup id="cite_ref-30" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-30">&#91;30&#93;</a></sup> the B.M.T. (short for "Biggest, Meatiest, Tastiest"), contains <a href="/wiki/Pepperoni" title="Pepperoni">pepperoni</a>, <a href="/wiki/Salami" title="Salami">salami</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Ham" title="Ham">ham</a>. The name originally stood for <a href="/wiki/Brooklyn-Manhattan_Transit_Corporation" class="mw-redirect" title="Brooklyn-Manhattan Transit Corporation">Brooklyn Manhattan Transit</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-31" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-31">&#91;31&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>Subway also sells <a href="/wiki/Breakfast_sandwich" title="Breakfast sandwich">breakfast sandwiches</a>, <a href="/wiki/English_muffin" title="English muffin">English muffins</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Flatbread" title="Flatbread">flatbread</a>. In 2006, "personal pizzas" debuted in some US markets. These are <a href="/wiki/Build_to_order" title="Build to order">made to order</a> (like the subs) and heated for 85 seconds. Breakfast and pizza items are only available in some stores. In November 2009, Subway signed a deal to serve exclusively <a href="/wiki/Seattle%27s_Best_Coffee" title="Seattle&#39;s Best Coffee">Seattle's Best Coffee</a> coffee as part of its breakfast menu in the US.<sup id="cite_ref-32" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-32">&#91;32&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>A 2009 <a href="/wiki/Zagat" title="Zagat">Zagat</a> survey named Subway the best provider of "Healthy Options" (in the "Mega Chain" category). Subway was also first in "Top Service" and "Most Popular" rankings. It placed second in "Top Overall", behind <a href="/wiki/Wendy%27s" title="Wendy&#39;s">Wendy's</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-33" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-33">&#91;33&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>On April 18, 2017, Subway announced the addition of paninis to its menu. Chipotle Steak &amp; Cheese, Triple Cheese, Chicken Cordon Bleu, and Italian B.M.T. Melt were the four variations announced.<sup id="cite_ref-34" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-34">&#91;34&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>On September 21, 2018, Subway debuted the Chipotle Cheesesteak sandwich for a limited-time. Regional testing of a crispy chicken sandwich also began taking place in Arkansas.<sup id="cite_ref-35" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-35">&#91;35&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Regional_variations">Regional variations</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Subway_(restaurant)&amp;action=edit&amp;section=4" title="Edit section: Regional variations">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>Subway's menu varies between countries, most significantly where there are religious requirements relating to the meats served.
</p><p>In 2006, the first <a href="/wiki/Kosher_Subway" class="mw-redirect" title="Kosher Subway">kosher Subway</a> restaurant in the United States opened, in a suburb of <a href="/wiki/Cleveland,_Ohio" class="mw-redirect" title="Cleveland, Ohio">Cleveland, Ohio</a> in the Mandel JCC of Cleveland. Former Subway spokesman <a href="/wiki/Jared_Fogle" title="Jared Fogle">Jared Fogle</a> attended the opening. A <a href="/wiki/Press_release" title="Press release">press release</a> stated, "With slight modifications, such as no pork-based products, and the use of <a href="/wiki/Soy_cheese" class="mw-redirect" title="Soy cheese">soy-based cheese</a> product, the menu is virtually identical to that of any other Subway restaurant."<sup id="cite_ref-36" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-36">&#91;36&#93;</a></sup> Other openings soon followed, briefly making Subway one of the largest U.S. kosher restaurant chains.<sup id="cite_ref-37" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-37">&#91;37&#93;</a></sup> At their peak, twelve kosher Subway locations were open in the U.S, including Kansas City and 5 in New York. As of 2011, only five remained: in Cleveland, <a href="/wiki/Miami" title="Miami">Miami</a>, <a href="/wiki/Los_Angeles" title="Los Angeles">Los Angeles</a>, and two stores in <a href="/wiki/Maryland" title="Maryland">Maryland</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-franchise_38-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-franchise-38">&#91;38&#93;</a></sup> Franchisees who failed noted a lack of support from the parent location in advertising, higher costs of kosher food and supervision, the inability to remain open on Saturdays, and that customers who do not keep kosher prefer the original menu and prices.<sup id="cite_ref-franchise_38-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-franchise-38">&#91;38&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>Subway opened its first restaurant in <a href="/wiki/India" title="India">India</a> in 2001 in <a href="/wiki/New_Delhi" title="New Delhi">New Delhi</a>. In deference to <a href="/wiki/Hindu" class="mw-redirect" title="Hindu">Hindu</a> and <a href="/wiki/Muslim" class="mw-redirect" title="Muslim">Muslim</a> beliefs, Subway restaurants in India do not serve <a href="/wiki/Beef" title="Beef">beef</a> or <a href="/wiki/Pork" title="Pork">pork</a> products; on the other hand, the country's large number of vegetarians has induced Subway's Indian outlets to offer a much extended range of vegetarian options. As of January 2017 there were 591 Subway restaurants in 68 Indian cities.<sup id="cite_ref-39" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-39">&#91;39&#93;</a></sup> On September 4, 2012, Subway opened its first all-vegetarian outlet on the campus of <a href="/wiki/Lovely_Professional_University" title="Lovely Professional University">Lovely Professional University</a> (LPU) in <a href="/wiki/Jalandhar" title="Jalandhar">Jalandhar</a>, <a href="/wiki/Punjab,_India" title="Punjab, India">Punjab</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-40" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-40">&#91;40&#93;</a></sup> On March 6, 2013, Subway opened its second all-vegetarian outlet also offering Jain food in <a href="/wiki/Paldi" title="Paldi">Paldi</a>, <a href="/wiki/Ahmedabad" title="Ahmedabad">Ahmedabad</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-41" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-41">&#91;41&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Nutritional_content">Nutritional content</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Subway_(restaurant)&amp;action=edit&amp;section=5" title="Edit section: Nutritional content">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>In 2011, Subway introduced gluten-free bread and brownies to some locations in Texas.<sup id="cite_ref-42" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-42">&#91;42&#93;</a></sup> It also cut the salt content of its sandwiches by 15 percent.<sup id="cite_ref-43" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-43">&#91;43&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>In the United Kingdom and Ireland, Subway has reduced salt content across its entire range by 33% and has committed to further reductions, in line with government targets.<sup id="cite_ref-44" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-44">&#91;44&#93;</a></sup> Subway's range of "Low Fat" subs is endorsed by the charity <a href="/wiki/Heart_Research_UK" title="Heart Research UK">Heart Research UK</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-45" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-45">&#91;45&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Marketing">Marketing</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Subway_(restaurant)&amp;action=edit&amp;section=6" title="Edit section: Marketing">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Subway2.JPG" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/90/Subway2.JPG/220px-Subway2.JPG" decoding="async" width="220" height="165" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/90/Subway2.JPG/330px-Subway2.JPG 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/90/Subway2.JPG/440px-Subway2.JPG 2x" data-file-width="2048" data-file-height="1536" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Subway2.JPG" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Subway in <a href="/wiki/Belo_Horizonte" title="Belo Horizonte">Belo Horizonte</a>, Brazil, in 2009</div></div></div>
<p>Subway is the second-biggest <a href="/wiki/Fast_food_advertising" title="Fast food advertising">fast food advertiser</a> in the United States, behind only <a href="/wiki/McDonald%27s" title="McDonald&#39;s">McDonald's</a>. It spent US$516,000,000 on measurable advertising in 2011.<sup id="cite_ref-46" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-46">&#91;46&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>Subway used the advertising slogan "Eat Fresh", and focused on how its sandwiches were made from freshly baked bread and fresh ingredients, in front of customers to their exact specifications, by employees which Subway called "Subway Sandwich Artists".
</p><p>In 2005, Subway scrapped its "Sub Club" stamp promotion, citing a growing number of counterfeit stamps due to online auction sites and the increasing availability of high-quality printers.<sup id="cite_ref-47" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-47">&#91;47&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-48" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-48">&#91;48&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>In November 2007, Subway's US commercials featured the cartoon character <a href="/wiki/Peter_Griffin" title="Peter Griffin">Peter Griffin</a> (from FOX's <i><a href="/wiki/Family_Guy" title="Family Guy">Family Guy</a></i>) promoting its new Subway Feast sandwich.<sup id="cite_ref-49" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-49">&#91;49&#93;</a></sup> Subway has also used "instant win" games, based on the game <a href="/wiki/Scrabble" title="Scrabble">Scrabble</a>.
</p><p>Subway ran a <a href="/wiki/Product_placement" title="Product placement">product placement</a> campaign in the US TV series <i><a href="/wiki/Chuck_(TV_series)" title="Chuck (TV series)">Chuck</a></i> since its first season. As ratings dwindled in the second season, a campaign to "save Chuck" was launched for fans, encouraging them to purchase a footlong sub from Subway on April 27, 2009, the date of the season finale. Tony Pace, Subway's marketing officer, called it the best product placement the restaurant chain has done "in several years."<sup id="cite_ref-50" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-50">&#91;50&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>To celebrate National Sandwich Day on November 3, 2015, Subway offered a Buy One sandwich, Give One sandwich free promotion.<sup id="cite_ref-51" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-51">&#91;51&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>Subway has sponsored a number of sports events, particularly <a href="/wiki/NASCAR" title="NASCAR">NASCAR</a> races, including the <a href="/wiki/Subway_400" title="Subway 400">Subway 400</a> (2002–2004), <a href="/wiki/Subway_500" class="mw-redirect" title="Subway 500">Subway 500</a> (2003–2007), <a href="/wiki/Subway_Fresh_500" class="mw-redirect" title="Subway Fresh 500">Subway Fresh 500</a> (2005–2013) and the <a href="/wiki/Subway_Firecracker_250" class="mw-redirect" title="Subway Firecracker 250">Subway Firecracker 250</a> (2009–2016). Subway sponsored the <a href="/wiki/Subway_Super_Series" class="mw-redirect" title="Subway Super Series">Subway Super Series</a> <a href="/wiki/Ice_hockey" title="Ice hockey">ice hockey</a> tournament from 2009–2014.
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Jared_Fogle">Jared Fogle</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Subway_(restaurant)&amp;action=edit&amp;section=7" title="Edit section: Jared Fogle">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Jared_Fogle_(2007).jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/40/Jared_Fogle_%282007%29.jpg/220px-Jared_Fogle_%282007%29.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="222" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/40/Jared_Fogle_%282007%29.jpg/330px-Jared_Fogle_%282007%29.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/40/Jared_Fogle_%282007%29.jpg/440px-Jared_Fogle_%282007%29.jpg 2x" data-file-width="948" data-file-height="956" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Jared_Fogle_(2007).jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div><a href="/wiki/Jared_Fogle" title="Jared Fogle">Jared Fogle</a> in 2007</div></div></div>
<p><a href="/wiki/Jared_Fogle" title="Jared Fogle">Jared Fogle</a> was a national spokesman for the company in the US starting in January 2000, giving talks on healthy living and appearing in advertisements. Fogle first came to attention in his native <a href="/wiki/Indiana" title="Indiana">Indiana</a> by claiming that he lost over 200 pounds in part by eating at Subway. From 2008, he was featured less often as the company marketed with more emphasis on its "5 dollar footlong" campaign.<sup id="cite_ref-Yahoo!_52-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Yahoo!-52">&#91;52&#93;</a></sup> Subway attributed between one-third and one-half of its growth from 1998 to 2011 to Fogle, the equivalent of a tripling in size.<sup id="cite_ref-murray20130609_53-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-murray20130609-53">&#91;53&#93;</a></sup> Subway ended its relationship with Fogle in 2015 after he was charged with possession of <a href="/wiki/Child_pornography" title="Child pornography">child pornography</a> and illicit sexual conduct with a minor. After pleading guilty in August 2015, he was sentenced to more than 15 years in <a href="/wiki/Federal_prison" title="Federal prison">federal prison</a> three months later.<sup id="cite_ref-54" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-54">&#91;54&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-55" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-55">&#91;55&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-56" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-56">&#91;56&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>In December 2015, following the removal of Fogle from its marketing, Subway introduced a new marketing campaign, "Founded on Fresh". The campaign focuses on Subway's establishment and early history, and features <a href="/wiki/Fred_DeLuca" title="Fred DeLuca">Fred DeLuca</a>, as played by his son, Jonathan. The new campaign downplays the use of jingles and celebrity endorsements (besides "targeted" sports marketing), in favor of focusing upon the qualities of its products, and specific products. Chief advertising officer Chris Carroll explained that the focus on fat, calories, and weight loss were "what fresh used to be", and that the new campaign would focus more on the sourcing of Subway's ingredients, such as its phase-out of <a href="/wiki/Antibiotic_use_in_livestock" title="Antibiotic use in livestock">antibiotic-treated meat</a>. Carroll also explained that the new strategy was being developed prior to the controversy involving Fogle.<sup id="cite_ref-adage-foundedonfresh_57-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-adage-foundedonfresh-57">&#91;57&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h3><span id=".245_footlongs"></span><span class="mw-headline" id="$5_footlongs">$5 footlongs</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Subway_(restaurant)&amp;action=edit&amp;section=8" title="Edit section: $5 footlongs">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Further information: <a href="/wiki/Subway_$5_footlong_promotion" title="Subway $5 footlong promotion">Subway $5 footlong promotion</a></div>
<p>In 2008, Subway began to offer all foot-long submarine sandwiches (excluding premium and double-meat varieties) for five dollars, in the continental United States and Canada, as a "limited time only" promotion. "Five Dollar Footlongs" quickly became the company's most successful promotion ever.<sup id="cite_ref-58" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-58">&#91;58&#93;</a></sup> Upon the initial promotion's completion, customer response prompted Subway to create a permanent "$5 Footlong Everyday Value Menu" that offered some footlong sandwiches for $5. Since 2011, there has been a monthly rotating $5 footlong.<sup id="cite_ref-Yahoo!_52-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Yahoo!-52">&#91;52&#93;</a></sup>
In October 2011, a similar promotion was launched in the United Kingdom. Customers can buy one of nine subs and any drink for £3 (for a six-inch sub) or £5 (for a footlong).<sup id="cite_ref-59" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-59">&#91;59&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>In 2012, <a href="/wiki/San_Francisco" title="San Francisco">San Francisco</a> discontinued the five-dollar footlong promotion due to the higher cost of doing business in the city.<sup id="cite_ref-60" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-60">&#91;60&#93;</a></sup> From June 2014 to the end of that year, some Subway locations began discontinuing the $5 dollar promotion.<sup id="cite_ref-61" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-61">&#91;61&#93;</a></sup> On November 1, 2014, Subway discontinued the five-dollar footlong promotion, replacing it with the Simple $6 Menu which included a six-inch select with a drink and a choice of cookies or chips.<sup id="cite_ref-62" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-62">&#91;62&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-63" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-63">&#91;63&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>On February 4, 2016, all classic footlongs were declared to be set at a new cost of $6 each.<sup id="cite_ref-64" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-64">&#91;64&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>On January 1, 2018, the $5 promotion returned with a $4.99 footlong menu of five subs, at participating locations.<sup id="cite_ref-65" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-65">&#91;65&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-66" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-66">&#91;66&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-67" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-67">&#91;67&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>On September 9, 2018, Subway announced that they were going to discontinue the $5 footlong promotion. This would help them boost their franchise profits. <sup id="cite_ref-68" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-68">&#91;68&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Italian_Hero">Italian Hero</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Subway_(restaurant)&amp;action=edit&amp;section=9" title="Edit section: Italian Hero">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>In early 2017, Subway introduced its Italian Hero, and advertised it with a campaign describing it as an authentic Italian[-American] sandwich. Two comedic spots feature stereotypical Italian-American characters on and around the stoop of a New York / New Jersey tenement building, one including a cameo by sportscaster <a href="/wiki/Dick_Vitale" title="Dick Vitale">Dick Vitale</a>. Another ad features <a href="/wiki/Food_Network" title="Food Network">Food Network</a>'s <a href="/wiki/Jeff_Mauro" title="Jeff Mauro">Jeff Mauro</a>, the "Sandwich King", who is Italian-American,<sup id="cite_ref-69" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-69">&#91;69&#93;</a></sup> discussing the nature and role of the different Italian meats and other ingredients.<sup id="cite_ref-70" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-70">&#91;70&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-71" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-71">&#91;71&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-72" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-72">&#91;72&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-73" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-73">&#91;73&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-74" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-74">&#91;74&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-75" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-75">&#91;75&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Animal_welfare">Animal welfare</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Subway_(restaurant)&amp;action=edit&amp;section=10" title="Edit section: Animal welfare">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<p>On December 28, 2015, Subway released a commitment to transition to a 100% cage-free egg supply chain in North America by 2025.<sup id="cite_ref-Steele_2015_76-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Steele_2015-76">&#91;76&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>On April 28, 2017, Subway released a chicken welfare policy<sup id="cite_ref-77" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-77">&#91;77&#93;</a></sup> that states that by 2024 or sooner, 100% of its U.S. chicken products will be produced in alignment with Global Animal Partnership (GAP) standards for higher welfare breeds, enhanced living environments (including lighting, litter, and enrichment), increased activity levels and optimized stocking density, and improved slaughter methods. To ensure compliance, Subway’s chicken suppliers will be third-party audited with updates communicated annually.<sup id="cite_ref-78" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-78">&#91;78&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>The policy announcement followed a nationwide campaign led by high school animal activist Lia Hyman in coordination with the animal protection NGO The Humane League.<sup id="cite_ref-79" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-79">&#91;79&#93;</a></sup> On April 20, 2017, Hyman and a group of activists traveled to Subway’s global headquarters in Connecticut to deliver more than 53,000 signatures from campaign supporters and held a demonstration outside the building after they were denied entry.<sup id="cite_ref-80" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-80">&#91;80&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>On March 18, 2019, Subway announced that it was transitioning to using only cage-free eggs through its Asia restaurants,<sup id="cite_ref-81" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-81">&#91;81&#93;</a></sup> making it the first major fast food brand to issue such a commitment in Asia. The announcement came after a campaign and investigation into Subway's Asia egg supply chain by NGO Lever Foundation.<sup id="cite_ref-82" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-82">&#91;82&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-83" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-83">&#91;83&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-84" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-84">&#91;84&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-85" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-85">&#91;85&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Controversies">Controversies</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Subway_(restaurant)&amp;action=edit&amp;section=11" title="Edit section: Controversies">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Hepatitis_A_contamination">Hepatitis A contamination</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Subway_(restaurant)&amp;action=edit&amp;section=12" title="Edit section: Hepatitis A contamination">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>In September 1999, at least 32 customers in <a href="/wiki/Seattle" title="Seattle">Seattle</a> contracted <a href="/wiki/Hepatitis_A" title="Hepatitis A">hepatitis A</a> after eating food contaminated with the virus at two Subway outlets.<sup id="cite_ref-columbian_86-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-columbian-86">&#91;86&#93;</a></sup> The virus, which is spread by eating or drinking food or water contaminated with infected feces, infects the liver causing nausea, vomiting, diarrhea, fatigue, and fever.<sup id="cite_ref-87" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-87">&#91;87&#93;</a></sup> Subsequent investigations found that staff failed to adhere to thorough hand washing and the use of plastic gloves during food preparation.<sup id="cite_ref-seattletimes_88-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-seattletimes-88">&#91;88&#93;</a></sup> A class-action lawsuit on behalf of 31 victims was resolved for $1.6 million.<sup id="cite_ref-89" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-89">&#91;89&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-90" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-90">&#91;90&#93;</a></sup> The most seriously affected victim—a 6-year-old boy—suffered acute liver failure and required a <a href="/wiki/Liver_transplantation" title="Liver transplantation">liver transplant</a>. He was awarded $10 million in an out-of-court settlement in 2001.<sup id="cite_ref-seattletimes_88-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-seattletimes-88">&#91;88&#93;</a></sup> A previous outbreak of hepatitis A in 1996 had also involved a Subway outlet in Seattle, although no legal action had resulted.<sup id="cite_ref-columbian_86-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-columbian-86">&#91;86&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>In April 2015, the <a href="/wiki/State_health_agency" title="State health agency">Arkansas Department of Health</a> issued a warning to the public that customers who had eaten at the Subway outlet in <a href="/wiki/Morrilton,_Arkansas" title="Morrilton, Arkansas">Morrilton, Arkansas</a>, may have been exposed to infection after an employee tested positive for the virus.<sup id="cite_ref-91" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-91">&#91;91&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-92" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-92">&#91;92&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Sandwich_size">Sandwich size</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Subway_(restaurant)&amp;action=edit&amp;section=13" title="Edit section: Sandwich size">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>On February 2, 2007, <a href="/wiki/KNXV" class="mw-redirect" title="KNXV">KNXV-TV</a> (with the help of the Arizona Department of Weights and Measures) reported that three of Subway's "Giant Sub" sandwiches, nominally each 3-foot (91&#160;cm) long, were actually 2&#160;feet 8&#160;inches (81&#160;cm), 2&#160;feet 8.25&#160;inches (81.92&#160;cm), and 2&#160;feet 8.5&#160;inches (82.6&#160;cm) long. The maximum variance in length allowed in Arizona is 3% (1.08 inches (2.7&#160;cm), for a three-foot sub). The report also showed the boxes designed to store these sandwiches were 2&#160;feet 10.75&#160;inches (88.27&#160;cm) in length; shorter than the maximum allowable variance. In response to the report, Subway said it was reevaluating its advertising, training and packaging materials with regard to the specific or implied length of Giant Subs, and was advising its franchisees to only discuss with customers the approximate number of expected servings and not a specific length of measurement.<sup id="cite_ref-93" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-93">&#91;93&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>In January 2013, an Australian teen, Matt Corby, complained on <a href="/wiki/Facebook" title="Facebook">Facebook</a> that Subway's "footlong" sandwich was only 11 inches (28&#160;cm) long, rather than 1 foot (30&#160;cm). Subway responded by saying, "With regards to the size of the bread and calling it a footlong, 'Subway Footlong' is a registered trademark as a descriptive name for the sub sold in Subway Restaurants and not intended to be a measurement of length."<sup id="cite_ref-94" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-94">&#91;94&#93;</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Discovery_(law)" title="Discovery (law)">Discovery</a> during a subsequent class-action lawsuit revealed that most Subway sandwiches were the advertised length. A $530,000 settlement was thrown out of court in 2017 for being "utterly worthless" to consumers.<sup id="cite_ref-95" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-95">&#91;95&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-96" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-96">&#91;96&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Franchise_relations">Franchise relations</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Subway_(restaurant)&amp;action=edit&amp;section=14" title="Edit section: Franchise relations">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>In 1995, Subway Sandwich Shops, Fred DeLuca, Peter Buck, and Doctor's Associates Inc. were held liable for breach of contract. An Illinois jury awarded more than $10 million in damages to Nicholas and Victoria Jannotta after finding lease and contract violations. The plaintiffs claimed the defendants had misrepresented the asset value of Subway Sandwich Shops (a leasing company used by Doctor's Associates for franchising purposes) while negotiating a 1985 lease agreement.<sup id="cite_ref-NationsRestaurantNews_97-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-NationsRestaurantNews-97">&#91;97&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>The U.S. House of Representatives' small business committee studied the franchise industry from 1992 to 1998. Dean Sagar noted, "Subway is the biggest problem in franchising and emerges as one of the key examples of every abuse you can think of."<sup id="cite_ref-FortuneMagazine_98-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FortuneMagazine-98">&#91;98&#93;</a></sup> In 1989, the U.S. Small Business Administration refused small business loans to Subway franchise owners until Subway removed a contract clause which gave it the power to seize and purchase any franchise without cause. <i><a href="/wiki/The_Dallas_Morning_News" title="The Dallas Morning News">The Dallas Morning News</a></i> reported Subway had seized American soldier Leon Batie Jr.'s Subway stores in 2006 while he was serving in Afghanistan.<sup id="cite_ref-DallasNews_99-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-DallasNews-99">&#91;99&#93;</a></sup> He had been deployed to support <a href="/wiki/Operation_Enduring_Freedom" title="Operation Enduring Freedom">Operation Enduring Freedom</a> in March 2005, three years after buying his first restaurant.<sup id="cite_ref-DallasNews_99-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-DallasNews-99">&#91;99&#93;</a></sup> Batie alleged Subway had violated the U.S. <a href="/wiki/Servicemembers_Civil_Relief_Act" title="Servicemembers Civil Relief Act">Servicemembers Civil Relief Act</a>. He filed a federal lawsuit against Subway, which was dismissed. He then filed suit in state court, in Dallas County, Texas. Both parties settled on "mutually agreeable" and confidential terms in January 2010.<sup id="cite_ref-100" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-100">&#91;100&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="United_Kingdom_VAT_treatment">United Kingdom VAT treatment</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Subway_(restaurant)&amp;action=edit&amp;section=15" title="Edit section: United Kingdom VAT treatment">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>In October 2010, Subway franchisees in the United Kingdom lost a high court appeal, against paying standard <a href="/wiki/Value-added_tax" title="Value-added tax">VAT</a> on all toasted subs, as required by <a href="/wiki/HM_Revenue_and_Customs" title="HM Revenue and Customs">HM Revenue and Customs</a>. Thus, in the United Kingdom, a toasted sub attracts VAT, whereas a cold sub, eaten off the premises, does not. Competitors such as <a href="/wiki/Quiznos" title="Quiznos">Quiznos</a> and <a href="/wiki/McDonald%27s" title="McDonald&#39;s">McDonald's</a> do not pay VAT on similar food.<sup id="cite_ref-101" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-101">&#91;101&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-102" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-102">&#91;102&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-103" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-103">&#91;103&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>In March 2012, <a href="/wiki/Chancellor_of_the_Exchequer" title="Chancellor of the Exchequer">Chancellor of the Exchequer</a>, <a href="/wiki/George_Osborne" title="George Osborne">George Osborne</a> announced plans to close the loophole that allows Subway competitors to offer hot food without paying VAT. This legislation was expected to come into force from October 2012 onward,<sup id="cite_ref-104" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-104">&#91;104&#93;</a></sup> but the government withdrew plans to charge VAT on originally hot food being allowed to cool naturally on May 28, 2012.<sup id="cite_ref-105" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-105">&#91;105&#93;</a></sup> In June 2012, Subway launched the "Toast the Tax" campaign to put pressure on <a href="/wiki/Government_of_the_United_Kingdom" title="Government of the United Kingdom">the government</a> to drop VAT on toasted sandwiches, as it has done for hot savouries.<sup id="cite_ref-106" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-106">&#91;106&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Footlong_trademark_disputes">Footlong trademark disputes</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Subway_(restaurant)&amp;action=edit&amp;section=16" title="Edit section: Footlong trademark disputes">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>On January 31, 2011, Subway lawyer Valerie Pochron, wrote to <a href="/wiki/Casey%27s_General_Stores" title="Casey&#39;s General Stores">Casey's General Stores</a>, a chain of Iowa-based convenience stores, demanding the small chain to cease using the term "footlong" in advertisements for its 12-inch sandwiches. Subway threatened to sue. Consequently, in February 2011, Casey's General Stores Inc. filed a petition in a U.S. District Court in <a href="/wiki/Des_Moines,_Iowa" title="Des Moines, Iowa">Des Moines</a>, seeking a legal declaration that the word "footlong" does not violate Subway's rights.<sup id="cite_ref-caseys_107-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-caseys-107">&#91;107&#93;</a></sup> Casey's further sought a declaration that the word "footlong" is a generic description of a sandwich measuring one foot.<sup id="cite_ref-108" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-108">&#91;108&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-109" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-109">&#91;109&#93;</a></sup> Before serving its complaint on Subway, Casey's voluntarily dismissed its action, ending the litigation.<sup id="cite_ref-110" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-110">&#91;110&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>Subway's trademark application for "footlong" has yet to be approved by the federal government. Subway has attempted to register it with the <a href="/wiki/United_States_Patent_and_Trademark_Office" title="United States Patent and Trademark Office">United States Patent and Trademark Office</a> twice. It filed on November 8, 2007,<sup id="cite_ref-111" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-111">&#91;111&#93;</a></sup> and June 4, 2009.<sup id="cite_ref-112" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-112">&#91;112&#93;</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Yum_Brands" class="mw-redirect" title="Yum Brands">Yum Brands</a> (KFC, Pizza Hut, Taco Bell and non-Canadian A&amp;W locations), Long John Silver's and other competitors are opposing that application.<sup id="cite_ref-caseys_107-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-caseys-107">&#91;107&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Ingredients">Ingredients</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Subway_(restaurant)&amp;action=edit&amp;section=17" title="Edit section: Ingredients">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>Subway made alterations to its bread after food blogger and activist <a href="/wiki/Vani_Hari" title="Vani Hari">Vani Hari</a> gathered more than 50,000 signatures in a <a href="/wiki/Petition" title="Petition">petition</a> drive. Subway removed <a href="/wiki/Azodicarbonamide" title="Azodicarbonamide">azodicarbonamide</a> from its bread.<sup id="cite_ref-113" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-113">&#91;113&#93;</a></sup> Before Vani Hari's petition, Subway had used azodicarbonamide as a bread conditioner, to whiten the dough and allow <a href="/wiki/Sandwich_bread" title="Sandwich bread">sandwich bread</a> to bake more quickly.  As of 2016<sup class="plainlinks noexcerpt noprint asof-tag update" style="display:none;"><a class="external text" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=Subway_(restaurant)&amp;action=edit">&#91;update&#93;</a></sup>, the ingredient was still used by other fast food restaurants.<sup id="cite_ref-114" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-114">&#91;114&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>In August 2015, Vani Hari again petitioned Subway in conjunction with <a href="/wiki/Natural_Resources_Defense_Council" title="Natural Resources Defense Council">Natural Resources Defense Council</a>, <a href="/wiki/Friends_of_the_Earth_(US)" title="Friends of the Earth (US)">Friends of the Earth</a>, the <a href="/wiki/Center_for_Food_Safety" title="Center for Food Safety">Center for Food Safety</a>, <a href="/wiki/Public_Interest_Research_Group" title="Public Interest Research Group">U.S. Public Interest Research Group</a> to commit to buying meat produced without the routine use of <a href="/wiki/Antibiotics" class="mw-redirect" title="Antibiotics">antibiotics</a> and to provide a timeline for doing so.<sup id="cite_ref-115" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-115">&#91;115&#93;</a></sup>  In October 2015, Subway announced it would transition to chicken raised without antibiotics in 2016 and turkey within the following 2–3 years, and would also transition beef and pork raised without antibiotics by 2025.<sup id="cite_ref-116" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-116">&#91;116&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-117" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-117">&#91;117&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Soy_protein_in_chicken_products">Soy protein in chicken products</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Subway_(restaurant)&amp;action=edit&amp;section=18" title="Edit section: Soy protein in chicken products">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>In an investigation by the <a href="/wiki/Canadian_Broadcasting_Corporation" title="Canadian Broadcasting Corporation">Canadian Broadcasting Corporation (CBC)</a>'s consumer affairs television series <i><a href="/wiki/Marketplace_(Canadian_TV_program)" title="Marketplace (Canadian TV program)">Marketplace</a></i> aired in February 2017, chicken from five fast food restaurants were lab-tested to determine constituents. While DNA testing found between 84.9% and 89.4% of the DNA from other restaurants' chicken products to be chicken DNA, with the remaining being unidentifiable plant DNA, on the two Subway chicken items tested, 53.6% and 42.8% of the DNA was found to be chicken, with the remainder being mostly soy. Although ingredients listings did show soy protein to be a constituent of both of the chicken products, Subway states that the proportion is less than or equal to 1%, and that the finding of about 50% soy DNA is not representative of the actual amount of soy in the product. Subway has called CBC's report "absolutely false and misleading" and demanded that it be retracted, a demand the CBC had not acceded to as of July&#160;2017<sup class="plainlinks noexcerpt noprint asof-tag update" style="display:none;"><a class="external text" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=Subway_(restaurant)&amp;action=edit">&#91;update&#93;</a></sup>. Meanwhile, however, Subway Canada stated that it was investigating with its supplier to ensure that the proportion of soy protein was as per expectations.<sup id="cite_ref-118" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-118">&#91;118&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-119" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-119">&#91;119&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-120" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-120">&#91;120&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-121" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-121">&#91;121&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-122" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-122">&#91;122&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>According to Subway's website, ingredients in U.S. stores may differ from ingredients in Canadian stores. Both countries include soy protein in chicken strips, but only the U.S. version states that it is present in quantities of 2% or less. The Canadian version includes soy as an ingredient in its chicken patty, but the United States version does not.<sup id="cite_ref-123" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-123">&#91;123&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>In April 2017, Subway sued the CBC, as well as the reporter and two producers, for $210 million, alleging the CBC acted "recklessly and maliciously", and that "these false statements... were published and republished, maliciously and without just cause or excuse, to a global audience, which has resulted in pecuniary loss to the plaintiffs." The CBC stood by its reports, stating that the DNA tests were done by independent and credible experts.<sup id="cite_ref-124" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-124">&#91;124&#93;</a></sup> The CBC's Emma Bédard stated that Subway has not provided any alternative explanation for the DNA test results obtained by the CBC.<sup id="cite_ref-torstar-cbcsuit_125-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-torstar-cbcsuit-125">&#91;125&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
